  alphabetical key order updated, security-rule paragraph
  rewritten to reflect the new field name. Added a paragraph
  explaining why the rename was necessary (collision with the
  existing `PairingInitiateResponse.broker_url`).

  ciphertext for the new key set. New ciphertext hex computed by
  running `AESGCM.encrypt` against the renamed AAD. Verified the
  resulting bytes against an independent Python encode.

  asserts the round-trip locally (needs Postgres for the rest of
  the test_crypto module to run — Postgres-less invocation: each
  vector function is pure).

## What's DEFERRED (would block 5a-2 commit by strict reading)

1. **Android `PairingRepository.complete(...)` UX flow.** The
   crypto module (`BootstrapEnvelope`) is in. The repository
   change to:
   - read `broker_url` + `bootstrap_key` + `bootstrap_key_signature`
     from the preview response,
   - verify the signature,
   - build the envelope,
   - POST to `sender_broker_url`,
   - show the manual-fallback banner on POST failure,
   is NOT in. The screen flow stays at the V1 manual code today.

2. **Server tests** for the new endpoint and the modified
   pairing routes (the 4 cases plan lists: bootstrap-key
   register success, bad signature, revoked sender, rotate).

3. **Optional FastAPI broker app** under `syncler[broker]` extra.
   `BrokerStorage` + `decrypt_bootstrap_envelope` ship in the
   base package; an `examples`-grade FastAPI mounting helper is
   not in. Production users can wire their own broker handler in
   ~30 lines using the helpers that are shipped.

4. **Integration-guide update** describing the automated flow.
   Spec is in `crypto-spec.md` §9 already; the user-facing
   walkthrough in `integration-guide.md` isn't updated yet.

Two options to consider:

**Option A**: Land Phase 5a-2 as a partial commit now, with
- the spec + vector rename,
- the server endpoint + schema/migration,

landing lands. Means the next commit ships a complete end-to-end
flow.

that won't move byte semantics. But the strict reading of the
protocol favors Option B.

## Plan deltas applied

### Delta 1 ג€” Naming collision: `sender_broker_url` (not `broker_url`)

`PairingInitiateResponse.broker_url` ALREADY EXISTS at
[schemas.py:313](D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/schemas.py:313)
and means "the Syncler-side broker URL that the QR encodes for
the device to scan." Reusing the name for the sender's
bootstrap-POST URL would silently overload existing wire
contract.

**New field name throughout 5a-2: `sender_broker_url`.**
- `PairingInitiateRequest.sender_broker_url: str | None = None`
  (signed in the canonical envelope when set)
- `PairingInitiateResponse.sender_broker_url: str | None = None`
  (echoed)
- `PairingPreviewResponse.sender_broker_url: str | None = None`
- `PendingPairing.sender_broker_url: Mapped[str | None]` (new
  nullable column)
- AAD field `sender_broker_url` (not `broker_url`) ג€” **note: this
  is a spec change against ֲ§9 of `docs/crypto-spec.md`. Spec
  edit required before code.**
- Python SDK: `client.create_pairing_qr(..., sender_broker_url=...)`

Same rename in the Android wire DTO, the SDK
`assemble_bootstrap_aad(...)` helper, the ֲ§9 test vector
(AAD JSON byte string changes because the key name changed,
which means the AEAD ciphertext vector and the canonical AAD
vector will need regeneration before commit).

### Delta 2 ג€” `/v1/pairing/complete` preserved and ordered correctly

The broker POST delivers `(user_id, pairing_key)` to the sender,
but `/v1/pairing/complete` is still what creates the Syncler-side
`Pairing` row and returns the `PairingCompleteResponse` fields
the device needs to populate its local `PairedSender`.

**Android post-confirm flow (revised order)**:

1. Generate local `pairingKey` (32 bytes via SecureRandom).
2. POST `/v1/pairing/complete` (existing path); receive
   `PairingCompleteResponse` with the canonical sender identity.
3. Verify the complete response sender identity matches the
   preview the user just confirmed (sanity check).
4. If preview carried `sender_broker_url` + `bootstrap_key` +
   `bootstrap_key_signature`:
   - Verify the bootstrap key signature against the sender's
     Ed25519 public key (fail loudly on mismatch ג€” treat as
     syncler-side substitution attack).
   - Build the bootstrap envelope.
   - POST to `sender_broker_url`.
5. Persist `PairedSender` locally (via existing
   `pairedSenderStore.add`).
6. If step 4's POST fails: keep the local pairing (it's
   already valid ג€” the user is paired) but surface the manual
   fallback banner so the sender's backend can be unblocked
   with a copy-paste.

**Key invariant**: Syncler `/v1/pairing/complete` MUST succeed
before the sender broker POST happens. Otherwise the sender
thinks pairing exists while Syncler rejected it.

Plan originally said "pairings row" ג€” code has
`PendingPairing` at
[models.py:239](D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/models.py:239)
for the initiate/preview state. Final `Pairing` row at

**`sender_broker_url` lives on `PendingPairing` only.** Not
copied to the final `Pairing` row. Audit log retains the
PendingPairing trail; the permanent Pairing row doesn't need
it (the bootstrap POST has already happened by then).

Migration `0008_pending_pairing_sender_broker.py`: add nullable
`sender_broker_url: Text` to `pending_pairings`.

Sender bootstrap-key columns stay on `senders` as planned

### Delta 4 ג€” FastAPI broker app is an optional SDK extra

Base `syncler` SDK stays FastAPI-free. The `make_broker_app(...)`
helper ships behind:

```toml

```

Install: `pip install syncler[broker]`.

`syncler/bootstrap.py` (decrypt helper) + `syncler/broker_storage.py`
(`BrokerStorage` protocol + `InMemoryBrokerStorage`) stay in the
base package ג€” they're pure logic. Only the FastAPI mounting

If broker extras isn't installed, `from syncler.broker import make_broker_app`
raises `ImportError` with a pointer to the extras install line.

Mirrors the `TemplateActionRunner` pattern (its own unauthenticated
client built locally, not the singleton with the auth interceptor).

## Phase 5a-1 ג€” Bootstrap protocol spec

### Goal

Replace today's manual flow ("user types `user_id` +
`pairing_key_hex` from the device screen into the sender's
backend") with an automated POST from the device to a sender-
operated broker URL. The pairing key never reaches the syncler
server in plain.

### Trust model

- **Sender**: trusted (it's the destination). Holds an Ed25519
  signing key (already exists in V1) and a NEW X25519 bootstrap
  public key (added in Phase 5a). The X25519 private key lives
  in the sender's backend, alongside its Ed25519 private key.
- **Syncler server**: treated as active-curious. Could attempt to
  substitute its own broker URL or its own X25519 key into the
  `pairing/preview` response. The protocol MUST detect either
  substitution via the sender's Ed25519 signature over the
  initiate payload.
- **Network between device and broker**: TLS protects in
  transit; HPKE-style envelope encryption protects against TLS
  termination at the syncler-server boundary or at a hostile
  CDN.
- **Device**: trusted endpoint of pairing; sees the pairing key
  in clear after decrypt.

### Key change: separate X25519 bootstrap key (NOT Ed25519ג†’X25519 conversion)

The sender registers **two** public keys with syncler:
- `signing_key` ג€” the existing Ed25519 public key (32 bytes).
  Unchanged from V1.
- `bootstrap_key` ג€” a new X25519 public key (32 bytes). The
  sender generates this once when it adopts the automated flow.

The sender SIGNS its X25519 bootstrap key with its Ed25519
signing key (`Ed25519.sign(signing_priv, "syncler-v1-bootstrap-key:" || bootstrap_pub_x25519)`)
and supplies the signature once at sender registration time (or
via a separate `/v1/senders/me/bootstrap-key` endpoint for
existing senders). The signature binds the bootstrap key to the
sender identity so syncler can't substitute its own key into
`pairing/preview`.

**Why separate keys instead of Ed25519ג†’X25519 conversion**:
- Library support is uneven. Python `cryptography` and Android's
  default crypto providers don't expose Ed25519ג†’X25519 conversion
  as first-class. Pulling in libsodium just for this is more
  surface area than adding a second key field.
- Audit clarity: the bootstrap operation has its own keypair, its
  own purpose, its own rotation lifecycle. Mixing key usage
  (signing AND key-agreement on the same long-term key) is
  conservative-bad-practice even when it's safe with proper
  domain separation.
- Operational flexibility: a sender can rotate the bootstrap key
  without rotating the signing key (or vice versa). V1.5+ will
  add explicit key rotation; making them independent up front
  keeps that option open.

### Wire flow

**Sender registers bootstrap key** (new endpoint, called once or
on rotation):

```
POST /v1/senders/me/bootstrap-key
Headers: signed by Ed25519 signing key (existing pattern)
Body: {
  "bootstrap_key": "<base64 X25519 pub, 32 bytes>",
  "bootstrap_key_signature": "<base64 Ed25519 sig over 'syncler-v1-bootstrap-key:' || bootstrap_key>"
}
```

Server verifies the Ed25519 signature, stores the X25519 pub key
on the `senders` row, and a hash `bootstrap_key_id =
SHA-256(bootstrap_key)[:16]` for stable identification.

**Sender initiates pairing** (extended existing endpoint):

```
POST /v1/pairing/initiate
Body (signed): {
  "sender_id": "...",
  "ttl_seconds": 300,
  "metadata": {...},
  "broker_url": "https://sender.example.com/syncler/bootstrap",  // NEW
}
Returns: {
  "pairing_id": "...",
  "pairing_token": "...",
  "broker_url": "<echoed back, server-validated>",
  "bootstrap_protocol_version": 1,
}
```

The `broker_url` is part of the sender-signed canonical envelope,
so syncler can't substitute its own value. If `broker_url` is
absent, the pairing falls back to the V1 manual flow.

**Server validates `broker_url` shape**:
- Release: `https://` only.
- Debug: `http://` allowed on private/LAN ranges (10.x, 172.16-31,
  192.168.x, localhost).
- No credentials in URL (`user:pass@host` rejected).
- No URL fragment.
- Length ג‰₪ 2048 chars.
- DNS resolvable (deferred; checked best-effort at pairing init).

**Device fetches preview** (existing endpoint, extended response):

```
GET /v1/pairing/preview?token=<pairing_token>
Returns: {
  "sender_id": "...",
  "sender_name": "...",
  "sender_public_key": "<base64 Ed25519 pub>",
  "sender_public_key_fingerprint": "...",
  "sender_name_hash": "...",
  "expires_at": "...",
  "broker_url": "<echoed>",                          // NEW
  "bootstrap_key": "<base64 X25519 pub, 32 bytes>",  // NEW
  "bootstrap_key_signature": "<base64 Ed25519 sig>", // NEW
  "bootstrap_protocol_version": 1,                   // NEW
}
```

Device verifies the bootstrap key signature against the sender's
Ed25519 public key BEFORE encrypting anything. If the verification
fails, the device refuses to proceed (treats it as syncler-side
key substitution).

**User confirms in the Android app.** The app builds the
bootstrap payload:

```
plaintext = JSON: {
  "user_id": "<uuid>",
  "pairing_key": "<base64 32 bytes>"
}
```

**Bootstrap encryption** (HPKE-style):

1. Device generates an ephemeral X25519 keypair `(eph_priv, eph_pub)`.
2. `shared_secret = X25519(eph_priv, sender.bootstrap_key)`.
3. `aead_key = HKDF-SHA256(salt=eph_pub || sender.bootstrap_key, ikm=shared_secret, info="syncler-v1-bootstrap-aead", length=32)`.
4. `nonce = 12 random bytes`.
5. `aad = JSON canonical bytes: {`
   `  "protocol_version": 1,`
   `  "pairing_id": "<uuid>",`
   `  "sender_id": "<uuid>",`
   `  "broker_url": "<echoed>",`
   `  "bootstrap_key_id": "<base64 16 bytes>",`
   `  "exp": "<ISO8601 UTC, 60s from now>"`
   `}`.
6. `ciphertext_with_tag = AES-256-GCM(aead_key, nonce, plaintext, aad)`.
7. Bootstrap envelope on wire (JSON):
   ```
   {
     "protocol_version": 1,
     "pairing_id": "...",
     "sender_id": "...",
     "bootstrap_key_id": "<base64>",
     "exp": "<ISO8601>",
     "ephemeral_pubkey": "<base64 32 bytes>",
     "nonce": "<base64 12 bytes>",
     "ciphertext": "<base64 ciphertext_with_tag>"
   }
   ```

AAD fields are reconstructed from a MIX of envelope fields and
broker-side trusted state, NOT just echoed from the envelope.
`protocol_version`, `pairing_id`, `sender_id`, `bootstrap_key_id`,
and `exp` come from the envelope (the client supplied them, AEAD
tag binds them). `broker_url` MUST come from the sender's stored
pairing state for `pairing_id`, created when the sender called
`pairing/initiate` ג€” never reconstructed from an untrusted source.
The broker MUST reject if the stored `broker_url` for that
`pairing_id` does not match byte-for-byte what the broker expects
to be in AAD. This is what stops a syncler-server substitution
attack: a hostile server could rewrite the AAD's `broker_url` in
the client-constructed AAD input to a value that matches the
wrong broker (note: `broker_url` is bound into AAD but never
emitted in the wire envelope); sourcing from sender-trusted
state on the broker side defeats that.

Canonicalization rules (binding to the spec):
- UUID fields (`pairing_id`, `sender_id`) are lowercase no-brace
  canonical (`str(uuid.UUID(value))` output).
- `broker_url` is the exact byte string signed in `pairing/initiate`
  and echoed in `pairing/preview`. Implementations MUST NOT
  lowercase, normalize, re-encode, or strip it before AAD
  assembly.
- `bootstrap_key_id` and other byte values use standard padded
  base64.
- AAD JSON encoder: `sort_keys=True, ensure_ascii=True,
  separators=(",", ":")` ג€” same as message AAD in ֲ§4 of
  `docs/crypto-spec.md`.

**Device POSTs the envelope** to `broker_url`:

```
POST {broker_url}
Content-Type: application/json
Body: <envelope above>
```

No `Authorization` header. The broker is sender-operated; the
sender authenticates by being able to decrypt. (The
`broker_url` itself is a sender-chosen secret if the sender
wants endpoint-based auth ג€” embed a token in the path.)

**Sender's broker handler**:

1. Validate envelope shape, parse JSON.
2. Reject if `exp` is more than 5 minutes in the past OR more
   than 5 minutes in the future relative to broker time. (The
   ֲ±5min window covers clock skew on both sides; the real
   replay guard is the compare-and-set on `pairing_id` at step
   10, not the `exp` field.)
3. Reject if `pairing_id` is unknown (sender's storage maps
   `pairing_id` ג†’ broker state created at `pairing/initiate`
   time, including the broker_url the sender supplied for that
   pairing). Important: this is sender-side validation; the
   sender's backend stores `pairing_id` after issuing the
   pairing init.
4. Reject if `bootstrap_key_id` ג‰  SHA-256(sender's
   bootstrap_pub)[:16] (key-rotation guard).
5. Reconstruct AAD bytes: take `protocol_version`, `pairing_id`,
   `sender_id`, `bootstrap_key_id`, `exp` from the envelope
   fields, AND take `broker_url` from the sender's STORED
   pairing state for this `pairing_id` (NOT from any envelope
   field ג€” a hostile server could rewrite that). Re-emit the
   AAD via the canonical JSON encoder (sort_keys, ensure_ascii,
   compact separators).
6. `shared_secret = X25519(sender.bootstrap_priv, envelope.ephemeral_pubkey)`.
7. `aead_key = HKDF-SHA256(salt=envelope.ephemeral_pubkey || sender.bootstrap_pub, ikm=shared_secret, info="syncler-v1-bootstrap-aead", length=32)`.
8. `AES-256-GCM-decrypt(aead_key, envelope.nonce, envelope.ciphertext, aad)`. Tag failure ג†’ reject 401.
9. Parse plaintext: `{user_id, pairing_key}`.
10. Compare-and-set into broker storage keyed on `pairing_id`:
    - If unset, store `(user_id, pairing_key)`. Return 201.
    - If already set with same `(user_id, pairing_key)`, return
      200 idempotently.
    - If already set with DIFFERENT values, return 409 (replay
      attack or conflicting request).

**SDK polling**:

```python
client.create_pairing_qr(ttl_seconds=300, broker_url="https://...")
pairing = client.wait_for_pairing(
    timeout_seconds=120,      # default
    poll_interval_seconds=1,  # default; jitter ֲ±20%
)
# pairing.user_id and pairing.pairing_key are now populated.
# Equivalent to set_pairing(...) being called automatically.
```

The SDK provides a default in-memory `BrokerStorage` for dev,
plus a `BrokerStorage` protocol so production users can wire it
to Redis / a DB. The SDK's `wait_for_pairing` polls the local
storage; the SDK does NOT call the syncler server during
bootstrap.

### Replay protection summary

- AAD binds `pairing_id`, `sender_id`, `broker_url`,
  `bootstrap_key_id`, `exp`, `protocol_version`.
- `pairing_id` is one-shot at the broker via compare-and-set ג€”
  this is the real replay stop, not the `exp` field.
- `exp` is set by the device to 60 seconds from build time as a
  nominal TTL. The broker accepts envelopes whose `exp` is
  within ֲ±5 minutes of broker wall time (clock-skew tolerance
  on both sides). The CAS at step 10 catches actual replay.
- A captured envelope replayed to the same broker hits the CAS
  guard (409 conflict, or 200 idempotent if the contents match).
- A captured envelope replayed to a DIFFERENT broker fails
  because `broker_url` is in AAD.
- A captured envelope replayed for a DIFFERENT pairing fails
  AAD verification.

### Network failure handling

If the device's POST to `broker_url` fails (timeout / 4xx / 5xx /
DNS / TLS), the Android app shows the V1 manual screen
(`user_id` + `pairing_key_hex`) with a banner: "automatic
pairing failed, see logs / enter manually." User can retry the
POST or copy/paste into the sender's backend. The manual flow
is NEVER removed ג€” automated pairing is a path on top of it, not
a replacement.

### Polling defaults

- `poll_interval_seconds`: 1.0
- `timeout_seconds`: 120
- Jitter: ֲ±20% of `poll_interval_seconds`
- Both configurable on `wait_for_pairing(...)`

### Test vectors

Phase 5a-1 ships crypto test vectors before any Android/SDK
code:

- HKDF context bytes for a known `(eph_pub, bootstrap_pub,
  shared_secret)` triple ג€” assert the derived `aead_key`.
- Full AEAD round-trip: known AAD JSON, known plaintext, known
  nonce, expected ciphertext.
- **Exact canonical bootstrap AAD JSON bytes** for a known
  `(protocol_version, pairing_id, sender_id, broker_url,
  bootstrap_key_id, exp)` tuple ג€” assert the byte string so SDK
  and host can't diverge silently. The vector MUST source
  `broker_url` from the sender's stored pairing state per the
  protocol rule above.
- Ed25519 signature over the bootstrap-key registration input.
  The input is the literal ASCII byte string
  `"syncler-v1-bootstrap-key:"` (24 bytes) concatenated with the
  **raw 32-byte X25519 public key** (NOT its base64 text). The
  vector asserts the signature over a known
  `(ed25519_seed, bootstrap_pub_raw)` pair.

Vectors land in `docs/crypto-spec.md` ֲ§9 (new), with `pytest`
assertion in `server/tests/test_crypto.py` and JUnit assertion
in `android/core/crypto/.../SpecVectorsTest.kt`.

## Phase 5a-2 ג€” Implementation

Server, Android, SDK code implementing the spec from 5a-1.
Triad cycle reviews the implementation against the spec.

**Out of scope for 5a-2** (deferred to V2 or later):
- Broker URL discovery from registered sender metadata (V1.5
  uses per-initiate `broker_url`).
- Sender bootstrap-key rotation UX.
- Push-based completion (broker pings SDK instead of polling).

## Phase 5b ג€” Full round-trip example

`examples/trading-bot/` becomes a directory with both sender and
plugin co-located:

```
examples/trading-bot/
  README.md       # rewritten; explicit about Python + Node dependencies
  bot.py          # sender side (existing); gains /api/ack + broker URL endpoint
  state.json      # extended with ack_count + ack_history (visible round-trip)
  plugin/
    src/plugin.ts
    manifest.json # UNSIGNED placeholders
    build.sh
    # dist/ and manifest.signed.json are gitignored
```

`/api/ack` mutates `state.json`:
- increments `ack_count`
- appends `{timestamp, item_id}` to `ack_history` (capped at 100
  entries, FIFO)

Plugin renders `payload.title` + `payload.body` + an "Acknowledge"
button that POSTs to `/api/ack`. After Phase 5a lands, the
sender side uses `wait_for_pairing(...)`.

## Phase 5c ג€” `npm create @syncler/plugin` scaffold

New package `create-plugin/` at the syncler monorepo root.
Published as `@syncler/create-plugin`. `npm create @syncler/plugin <name>`
runs it.

Interactive prompts:
- plugin id (regex-validated reverse-DNS)
- plugin name (human-readable)
- sender id (UUID ג€” paste from `client.register_if_needed()`)
- renderer (`script` | `template`, default `script`)
- card_type (`event` | `live`, default `event`)
- capabilities (multi-select: `network` / `storage` /
  `showNotification`)

Scaffold output:

```
my-plugin/
  src/plugin.ts              # BasePlugin subclass, defaults
  manifest.json              # UNSIGNED placeholders, fields filled
  build.sh
  package.json               # build / build:sign / publish scripts
  README.md                  # step-by-step instructions
  .gitignore                 # dist/, manifest.signed.json, *.pem
```

Plain template literals inside the Node script. No handlebars.
Tiny sender stub or pointer to `examples/trading-bot/`.

## Phase 5d ג€” Validator polish backlog (first batch)

Define what lands now vs later. **First batch** (this commit):

1. `minPlatformVersion` numeric component caps (6 digits each)
   ג€” match the existing `version` regex.
2. Action endpoint URL validation: HTTPS in release; http only
   for LAN private ranges in debug.
3. `template.fields` keys that aren't in the layout's allowed
   set: SDK rejects, instead of forwarding to the server's 422.
4. `cardKeyPath` full `$.field(.subfield)*` grammar
   (currently `startsWith("$")`).
5. Plugin `id` regex parity check: confirm the SDK regex matches
   the server's character class exactly.

**Deferred** (not in 5d, file in V1.5 DX #9 backlog):
- `card_key` ג†” `card_key_path` payload-side mismatch ג€” not pure
  manifest validation; needs payload sample or test convention.
- `template.actions.endpoint` glob-shape validation beyond
  HTTPS ג€” overlaps with #2; revisit if needed.

## Phase 5e ג€” Docs + roadmap update

Move V1.5 DX items 6ג€“9 from "planned" to "shipped" in
`docs/ROADMAP.md`. Add automated pairing protocol spec to
`docs/crypto-spec.md` (already drafted in 5a-1).
`docs/integration-guide.md` gains:
- ֲ§1 mention of automated pairing
- ֲ§8 (testing) updated walk-through
- Pointer to the full round-trip example
- Pointer to the `npm create` scaffold

## Disagreements resolved

| Topic | Codex | Gemini | Resolution |
|---|---|---|---|
| Encryption primitive | Separate X25519 bootstrap key | Ed25519ג†’X25519 conversion | **Separate X25519 key** (Codex) ג€” library friction + audit clarity outweighs the "standard" argument. |
| Spec/vectors before code | YES, gate 5a-2 on 5a-1 | Not raised explicitly | **YES** (Codex) ג€” matches the V1 pattern where Phase 0/1/2 each had spec agreement before code. |
| Broker URL location | `pairing/initiate` request (signed) | `pairing/preview` response | **Both** ג€” sender puts it in initiate (signed); server echoes in preview. |
| Polling interval | 1s / 120s with jitter | Not raised | **1s / 120s with ֲ±20% jitter** (Codex). |
| Replay token mechanism | AAD binding only; avoid server-issued HMAC token | (Not specified) | **AAD binding** (Codex). The Syncler server is not on the bootstrap trust path; adding a token it knows would weaken that boundary. |

## Out of scope for the whole Phase 5 milestone

- Push-based pairing completion (broker pushes to SDK). Polling
  is fine for V1.5; push is a V2 add.
- Sender key rotation UX (bootstrap key OR Ed25519). Manual
  rotation works; guided UX is V1.5+.
- Marketplace plugin distribution. V1 + V1.5 stay sideload-only.
- Mobile pairing UX redesign (animated progress, etc.). The
  current screen gets a banner + fallback affordance; full UX
  polish is V2.

.triad\65-codex-log.txt:175:docs/integration-guide.md:5:Syncler does not know what your data looks like, what your UI says, or what your buttons do. Your payload, your plugin code (or template manifest), your callback endpoint — Syncler just routes bytes.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:176:docs/integration-guide.md:12:- **Template** (`renderer: "template"`) — no JavaScript. You ship a small JSON manifest that maps fields out of your payload via JSONPath (`$.title`, `$.body.summary`) into a native Material 3 card. Buttons are host-rendered and the host POSTs the decrypted payload to the action's declared endpoint. Faster, lighter, no JS attack surface; constrained to a fixed set of layouts.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:177:docs/integration-guide.md:14:And one of two delivery modes:
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:178:docs/integration-guide.md:16:- **Event** (`card_type: "event"`) — the default. Each `send_to` produces a new immutable inbox row. Good for notifications, alerts, transactional events.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:179:docs/integration-guide.md:17:- **Live** (`card_type: "live"`) — persistent, upsertable. Subsequent upserts to the same `card_key` replace the previous payload (highest `sequence_number` wins). Good for status cards that change over time (delivery progress, market position, sensor reading). Server-enforced 48h TTL; you re-upsert to extend.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:180:docs/integration-guide.md:21:The Syncler inbox shows a *native* row for every message — sender name, title, subtitle, summary, arrival time — pulled from the `hostPreview` block you embed in your payload (§2). The detail view that opens on tap is what your script bundle's `render()` or your template manifest produces.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:181:docs/integration-guide.md:27:- **Native row rendering** from your `hostPreview` block (title / subtitle / summary) plus the server's arrival time (HH:mm for today, MMM d for older).
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:182:docs/integration-guide.md:30:- **Inbox search** (case-insensitive substring) over title, subtitle, summary, sender name, AND any tokens you supplied in `hostPreview.searchText`.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:183:docs/integration-guide.md:35:- **Live cards pin above events.** When mixed in the same inbox, live cards (`card_type: "live"`) sort above event cards (`card_type: "event"`), each subsorted by recency. The "Live" view in the drawer shows only live cards.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:184:docs/integration-guide.md:36:- **Cross-device dismiss.** When the user dismisses a message on device A, the server marks `DeliveryStatus.dismissed_at` for that device. Device B's next inbox pull (driven by the `dismiss` SSE event or a fresh refresh) excludes the dismissed row — `inbox_for_device` LEFT JOINs `DeliveryStatus` and filters `dismissed_at IS NULL`. Per-device dismiss, server-side.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:185:docs/integration-guide.md:37:- **Real-time hints over SSE.** Foreground devices keep an authenticated Server-Sent Events stream open to `/v1/events`. The server pushes content-blind hints — `inbox.changed`, `state.changed`, `dismiss`, `card.upsert`, `card.delete` — and the client re-fetches over REST in response. The actual payloads still flow over the existing pull endpoints; SSE is the wakeup signal, not the data channel. Backgrounded devices fall back to FCM.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:186:docs/integration-guide.md:39:You don't need to opt into any of these. Populate `hostPreview` and they all work.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:187:docs/integration-guide.md:45:Two parts: a reserved **`hostPreview`** block the platform renders natively as the inbox row, and the rest of the payload that your plugin's `render()` consumes for the detail view.

.triad\65-codex-log.txt:214:docs/integration-guide.md:281:**Actions.** Each action is a button on the card. When tapped, the host POSTs the **full decrypted payload as `application/json`** to `endpoint`. No `Authorization` header is attached — the host explicitly uses an unauthenticated HTTP client for action POSTs so the user's Syncler bearer token never reaches your plugin endpoint (security boundary). If you need request authentication, HMAC the body using a sender-specific secret your backend knows out of band, or rely on TLS + endpoint allowlisting alone.

.triad\65-codex-log.txt:248:docs/integration-guide.md:464:8. The server pushes an `inbox.changed` event over the SSE stream the open app is subscribed to (foreground); the phone refreshes its inbox, decrypts the message, fetches your bundle (or applies your template manifest), and shows the native row within ~1s. If the app is backgrounded, FCM wakes it and the inbox refresh happens on the next foreground.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:249:docs/integration-guide.md:471:- **`410 plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender`** — `plugin_id` (the row UUID) is wrong, or you accidentally used `plugin_identifier`. The two are distinct (see §5 vs §6).
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:250:docs/integration-guide.md:472:- **`410 recipient has no active devices`** — the user has no enrolled device (signed up but never opened the app, or revoked all devices). FCM availability is *not* required; messages are stored regardless and pulled via `/v1/messages/inbox`.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:251:docs/integration-guide.md:473:- **`409 nonce already used`** — your code reused a nonce somehow; SDK generates fresh nonces per `send_to`, so this means you're calling `send_to` with cached envelope bytes. Rebuild.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:252:docs/integration-guide.md:475:- **`410 plugin missing, revoked, not live-type, or not owned by sender`** (cards upsert) — the plugin row's `card_type` isn't `"live"`, or the row has a non-null `revoked_at`, or the publish row's `sender_id` doesn't match the signed envelope's sender. The error message is intentionally generic so a probing caller can't distinguish the cases (don't leak which plugin UUIDs exist).
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:253:docs/integration-guide.md:476:- **`410 no active pairing`** (cards upsert) — the recipient user has not paired with your sender, or the pairing has been revoked. The user needs to re-scan your pairing QR.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:254:docs/integration-guide.md:477:- **`400 expires_at exceeds the 48h live-card cap`** (cards upsert) — your supplied `expires_at` is more than 48 hours from now. Live cards are capped server-side to prevent slot squatting. Send shorter and re-upsert to extend.
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:255:docs/integration-guide.md:478:- **`400 expires_at is not in the future`** (cards upsert) — you sent an already-expired `expires_at`. Use a future timestamp.

The server pushes content-blind hints — `inbox.changed`, `state.changed`, `dismiss`, `card.upsert`, `card.delete` — and the client re-fetches over REST in response. The actual payloads still flow over the existing pull endpoints; SSE is the wakeup signal, not the data channel. Backgrounded devices fall back to FCM.

.triad\65-codex-log.txt:458:.\docs\integration-guide.md:425:**Script renderer** — your `onclick` handler builds the body via `platform.network.fetch`. In the §3 example that's:
.triad\65-codex-log.txt:459:.\docs\integration-guide.md:434:**Template renderer** — the host POSTs the **full decrypted payload** as the body, verbatim. There's no JS hook to intervene. Your endpoint receives the whole payload JSON; pull whatever fields you need server-side. If you need request authentication, HMAC the payload using a sender-specific secret your backend shares out of band with itself, or rely on TLS + endpoint allowlisting alone.

For template renderer, your `card_key` (or any other field in the payload) serves the same dedupe role. Dedupe by `item_id` / `card_key` alone if a single tap is what you care about.

If the app is backgrounded, FCM wakes it and the inbox refresh happens on the next foreground.

.triad\65-codex-log.txt:1155:.\docs\integration-guide.md:464:8. The server pushes an `inbox.changed` event over the SSE stream the open app is subscribed to (foreground); the phone refreshes its inbox, decrypts the message, fetches your bundle (or applies your template manifest), and shows the native row within ~1s. If the app is backgrounded, FCM wakes it and the inbox refresh happens on the next foreground.

.triad\66-codex-log.txt:992:docs/integration-guide.md:36:- **Per-device dismiss (server-side filter).** When the user dismisses a message on device A, `/v1/messages/{id}/dismiss` writes a `DeliveryStatus` row keyed on `(message_id, device_id=A)`. Subsequent calls to `/v1/messages/inbox` from device A LEFT JOIN `DeliveryStatus` for `device_id=A` and filter rows where `dismissed_at IS NOT NULL` out of A's feed. The dismiss SSE event still fans out to *all* of the user's devices, but the server-side filter is per-device — devices B, C, etc. receive the hint and refresh, but their own feeds keep the row until they dismiss it themselves. V1 design: dismiss is a per-device gesture (some users want a card visible elsewhere); cross-device "dismiss everywhere" is a V1.5 add.
.triad\66-codex-log.txt:993:docs/integration-guide.md:37:- **Real-time hints over SSE.** Foreground devices keep an authenticated Server-Sent Events stream open to `/v1/events`. The server pushes content-blind hints — `inbox.changed`, `state.changed`, `dismiss`, `card.upsert`, `card.delete` — and the client re-fetches over REST in response. The actual payloads still flow over the existing pull endpoints; SSE is the wakeup signal, not the data channel. Backgrounded devices fall back to FCM.

.triad\66-codex-log.txt:1026:docs/integration-guide.md:371:**`card_key` must equal `card_key_path` resolved on the plaintext.** The manifest's `card_key_path` (declared at publish time, e.g. `"$.order_id"`) is the path the host extracts on decrypt to use as the merge key for this card. The `card_key` you pass to `upsert_card` is what the server stores. If the two disagree, the host's per-card merge breaks and your "live" card behaves like a series of event cards. The server doesn't cross-check the two — enforcement is your responsibility. (V1 validates `card_key_path` only as `startswith("$")`; a future phase will tighten this to the full `$.field(.subfield)*` JSONPath grammar used by template fields.)

.triad\66-codex-log.txt:1379:docs/integration-guide.md:37:- **Real-time hints over SSE.** Foreground devices keep an authenticated Server-Sent Events stream open to `/v1/events`. The server pushes content-blind hints — `inbox.changed`, `state.changed`, `dismiss`, `card.upsert`, `card.delete` — and the client re-fetches over REST in response. The actual payloads still flow over the existing pull endpoints; SSE is the wakeup signal, not the data channel. Backgrounded devices fall back to FCM.

.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1758:docs/integration-guide.md:5:Syncler does not know what your data looks like, what your UI says, or what your buttons do. Your payload, your plugin code (or template manifest), your callback endpoint — Syncler just routes bytes.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1759:docs/integration-guide.md:12:- **Template** (`renderer: "template"`) — no JavaScript. You ship a small JSON manifest that maps fields out of your payload via JSONPath (`$.title`, `$.body.summary`) into a native Material 3 card. Buttons are host-rendered and the host POSTs the decrypted payload to the action's declared endpoint. Faster, lighter, no JS attack surface; constrained to a fixed set of layouts.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1760:docs/integration-guide.md:16:- **Event** (`card_type: "event"`) — the default. Each `send_to` produces a new immutable inbox row. Good for notifications, alerts, transactional events.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1761:docs/integration-guide.md:17:- **Live** (`card_type: "live"`) — persistent, upsertable. Subsequent upserts to the same `card_key` replace the previous payload (highest `sequence_number` wins). Good for status cards that change over time (delivery progress, market position, sensor reading). Server-enforced 48h TTL; you re-upsert to extend.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1762:docs/integration-guide.md:21:The Syncler inbox shows a *native* row for every message — sender name, title, subtitle, summary, arrival time — pulled from the `hostPreview` block you embed in your payload (§2). The detail view that opens on tap is what your script bundle's `render()` or your template manifest produces.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1763:docs/integration-guide.md:35:- **Live cards pin above events.** When mixed in the same inbox, live cards (`card_type: "live"`) sort above event cards (`card_type: "event"`), each subsorted by recency. The "Live" view in the drawer shows only live cards.

.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1780:docs/integration-guide.md:315:Live cards work with **either** renderer. The most common combo is `renderer="template"` + `card_type="live"` (delivery progress card with no JS).
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1781:docs/integration-guide.md:329:# `card_key_path="$.order_id"` resolves to and MUST equal the `card_key`
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1782:docs/integration-guide.md:375:**`card_key` must equal `card_key_path` resolved on the plaintext.** The manifest's `card_key_path` (declared at publish time, e.g. `"$.order_id"`) is the path the host extracts on decrypt to use as the merge key for this card. The `card_key` you pass to `upsert_card` is what the server stores. If the two disagree, the host's per-card merge breaks and your "live" card behaves like a series of event cards. The server doesn't cross-check the two — enforcement is your responsibility. (V1 validates `card_key_path` only as `startswith("$")`; a future phase will tighten this to the full `$.field(.subfield)*` JSONPath grammar used by template fields.)
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1783:docs/integration-guide.md:382:- **Plugin must be active and live-type.** `Plugin.revoked_at IS NULL` and `card_type = "live"`; otherwise 410.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1784:docs/integration-guide.md:464:Note: the platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body for you in V1. If you need to distinguish which device acted, include a sender-generated identifier in your payload and (for script renderer) have the plugin echo it back. For template renderer, your `card_key` (or any other field in the payload) serves the same dedupe role. Dedupe by `item_id` / `card_key` alone if a single tap is what you care about.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1785:docs/integration-guide.md:492:8. The server pushes an `inbox.changed` event over the SSE stream the open app is subscribed to (foreground); the phone refreshes its inbox, decrypts the message, fetches your bundle (or applies your template manifest), and shows the native row within ~1s. If the app is backgrounded, FCM wakes it and the inbox refresh happens on the next foreground.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1786:docs/integration-guide.md:503:- **`410 plugin missing, revoked, not live-type, or not owned by sender`** (cards upsert) — the plugin row's `card_type` isn't `"live"`, or the row has a non-null `revoked_at`, or the publish row's `sender_id` doesn't match the signed envelope's sender. The error message is intentionally generic so a probing caller can't distinguish the cases (don't leak which plugin UUIDs exist).
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1949:docs/integration-guide.md:5:Syncler does not know what your data looks like, what your UI says, or what your buttons do. Your payload, your plugin code (or template manifest), your callback endpoint — Syncler just routes bytes.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1950:docs/integration-guide.md:12:- **Template** (`renderer: "template"`) — no JavaScript. You ship a small JSON manifest that maps fields out of your payload via JSONPath (`$.title`, `$.body.summary`) into a native Material 3 card. Buttons are host-rendered and the host POSTs the decrypted payload to the action's declared endpoint. Faster, lighter, no JS attack surface; constrained to a fixed set of layouts.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1951:docs/integration-guide.md:16:- **Event** (`card_type: "event"`) — the default. Each `send_to` produces a new immutable inbox row. Good for notifications, alerts, transactional events.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1952:docs/integration-guide.md:17:- **Live** (`card_type: "live"`) — persistent, upsertable. Subsequent upserts to the same `card_key` replace the previous payload (highest `sequence_number` wins). Good for status cards that change over time (delivery progress, market position, sensor reading). Server-enforced 48h TTL; you re-upsert to extend.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1953:docs/integration-guide.md:21:The Syncler inbox shows a *native* row for every message — sender name, title, subtitle, summary, arrival time — pulled from the `hostPreview` block you embed in your payload (§2). The detail view that opens on tap is what your script bundle's `render()` or your template manifest produces.
.triad\67-codex-log.txt:1954:docs/integration-guide.md:35:- **Live cards pin above events.** When mixed in the same inbox, live cards (`card_type: "live"`) sort above event cards (`card_type: "event"`), each subsorted by recency. The "Live" view in the drawer shows only live cards.

.triad\68-codex-log.txt:265:docs\integration-guide.md:275:**JSONPath dialect.** Only `$.field(.subfield)*` is accepted. No array indexing (`$.items[0]`), no wildcards (`$.*`), no filters (`$.items[?(@.x>0)]`). Field-name segments must match `[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*`. The server rejects manifests with malformed paths at publish time, and the client-side resolver returns `null` for malformed input as a defense-in-depth.

(V1 validates `card_key_path` only as `startswith("$")`; a future phase will tighten this to the full `$.field(.subfield)*` JSONPath grammar used by template fields.)
.triad\68-codex-log.txt:562:docs\integration-guide.md:385:- **Rate limit.** Fixed window of 60 upserts per minute per `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`; else 429. (There's also an IP-bucketed pre-auth limit of 120/min for cheap DoS protection.)
.triad\68-codex-log.txt:563:docs\integration-guide.md:394:    card_key="order-456",
.triad\68-codex-log.txt:564:docs\integration-guide.md:398:`user_id` is **required**. The canonical signed envelope binds `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)` — without `user_id` in the signature, an attacker (or a coincidence: two users with the same `card_key` under the same sender) could be deleted by mistake. The delete endpoint matches exactly that triple in the row lookup.

.triad\68-codex-log.txt:567:docs\integration-guide.md:464:Note: the platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body for you in V1. For template renderer, your `card_key` (or any other field in the payload) serves the same dedupe role. Dedupe by `item_id` / `card_key` alone if a single tap is what you care about.

.triad\68-codex-log.txt:3470:.\docs\integration-guide.md:275:**JSONPath dialect.** Only `$.field(.subfield)*` is accepted. No array indexing (`$.items[0]`), no wildcards (`$.*`), no filters (`$.items[?(@.x>0)]`). Field-name segments must match `[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*`. The server rejects manifests with malformed paths at publish time, and the client-side resolver returns `null` for malformed input as a defense-in-depth.

V1 design: dismiss is a per-device gesture (some users want a card visible elsewhere); cross-device "dismiss everywhere" is a V1.5 add.

Plugin-scoped *content* search (a search bar that runs against your backend) is V1.5.

.triad\69-codex-log.txt:738:.\docs\integration-guide.md:565:- **`UNSIGNED-PLACEHOLDER-REPLACE-WITH-SIGN-BUNDLE` in `bundleHash` / `signature`.** You forgot to run `sign-bundle.ts` on the built bundle. The SDK validator rejects this (post Phase 4.1) — `bundleHash` must be exactly 64 lowercase hex chars (SHA-256), `signature` must be exactly 128 hex chars (Ed25519). If the SDK lets it through, the server rejects at publish with 422; if both let it through, the device fails the manifest-hash check and shows "Plugin not loaded."
.triad\69-codex-log.txt:1157:.\docs\integration-guide.md:36:- **Per-device dismiss (server-side filter).** When the user dismisses a message on device A, `/v1/messages/{id}/dismiss` writes a `DeliveryStatus` row keyed on `(message_id, device_id=A)`.    9: import app.syncler.core.storage.PairedSenderStore
  10: import javax.inject.Inject
  11: import javax.inject.Singleton
  12: import retrofit2.HttpException
  13: import timber.log.Timber
  14: 
  15: /**
  16:  * Two-phase pairing flow (M6.1 fix per Codex+Gemini review):
  17:  *
  18:  *   1. parseBrokerUrl(url) -> PairingCandidate
  19:  *   2. preview(candidate) -> PairingPreviewResponseDto  [non-consuming]
  20:  *   3. user confirms fingerprint manually
  21:  *   4. confirm(candidate, preview, encryptedInitialState) -> PairedSender
  22:  *      ONLY at this point does the server consume the token and we
  23:  *      persist the local PairedSender record.
  24:  *
  25:  * cancel(candidate) is a no-op server-side (the token is left un-consumed
  26:  * and will expire on its TTL). Local state is never written until confirm.
  27:  */
  28: @Singleton
  29: class PairingRepository @Inject constructor(
  30:     private val api: SynclerApi,
  31:     private val pairedSenderStore: PairedSenderStore,
  32: ) {
  33:     fun parseBrokerUrl(url: String): PairingCandidate? {
  34:         // Debug builds accept plain http:// so devs can pair against a local
  35:         // broker without TLS. Release builds require HTTPS.
  36:         val schemeOk = url.startsWith("https://") || (BuildConfig.DEBUG && url.startsWith("http://"))
  37:         if (!schemeOk) {
  38:             Timber.tag(TAG).w("non-https broker URL rejected")
  39:             return null
  40:         }
  41:         val uri = runCatching { Uri.parse(url) }.getOrNull() ?: return null
  42:         val token = uri.getQueryParameter("token") ?: return null
  43:         return PairingCandidate(brokerUrl = url, pairingToken = token)
  44:     }
  45: 
  46:     suspend fun preview(candidate: PairingCandidate): Result<PairingPreviewResponseDto> =
  47:         runCatching { api.previewPairing(candidate.pairingToken) }
  48:             .onFailure {
  49:                 if (it is HttpException) Timber.tag(TAG).w("preview http %d", it.code())
  50:                 else Timber.tag(TAG).e(it, "preview error")
  51:             }
  52: 
  53:     suspend fun confirm(
  54:         candidate: PairingCandidate,
  55:         preview: PairingPreviewResponseDto,
  56:         pairingKey: ByteArray,
  57:         encryptedInitialState: ByteArray,
  58:     ): Result<PairedSender> = runCatching {
  59:         val response = api.completePairing(
  60:             PairingCompleteRequestDto(
  61:                 pairingToken = candidate.pairingToken,
  62:                 encryptedInitialState = Base64.encodeToString(
  63:                     encryptedInitialState,
  64:                     Base64.NO_WRAP,
  65:                 ),
  66:             ),
  67:         )
  68:         // Defense-in-depth: confirm the server's complete-response identity
  69:         // matches the preview the user manually confirmed across ALL identity
  70:         // fields (sender_id + public_key + fingerprint + name + name_hash).
  71:         // A backend bug or mid-stream swap that mutated even just the name
  72:         // would slip through a partial check.
  73:         if (response.senderId != preview.senderId ||
  74:             response.senderPublicKey != preview.senderPublicKey ||
  75:             response.senderPublicKeyFingerprint != preview.senderPublicKeyFingerprint ||
  76:             response.senderName != preview.senderName ||
  77:             response.senderNameHash != preview.senderNameHash
  78:         ) {
  79:             Timber.tag(TAG).e("preview/complete identity mismatch ג€” revoking and aborting")
  80:             val revoked = runCatching { api.revokePairing(response.pairingId) }
  81:             revoked.onFailure { Timber.tag(TAG).e(it, "failed to revoke after mismatch ג€” manual cleanup required") }
  82:             if (revoked.isSuccess && revoked.getOrNull()?.isSuccessful == false) {
  83:                 Timber.tag(TAG).e("revoke returned non-2xx after mismatch ג€” manual cleanup required")
  84:             }
  85:             throw IllegalStateException("preview/complete identity mismatch")
  86:         }
  87: 
  88:         val record = PairedSender(
  89:             pairingId = response.pairingId,
  90:             senderId = response.senderId,
  91:             senderName = response.senderName,
  92:             senderPublicKey = Base64.decode(response.senderPublicKey, Base64.NO_WRAP),
  93:             fingerprint = response.senderPublicKeyFingerprint,
  94:             nameHash = Base64.decode(response.senderNameHash, Base64.NO_WRAP),
  95:             firstPairedAt = response.pairedAt,
  96:             pairingKey = pairingKey,
  97:         )
  98:         pairedSenderStore.add(record)
  99:         record
 100:     }.onFailure { Timber.tag(TAG).e(it, "confirm error") }
 101: 
 102:     suspend fun revoke(pairingId: String): Result<Unit> = runCatching {
 103:         val response = api.revokePairing(pairingId)
 104:         if (!response.isSuccessful) throw HttpException(response)
 105:         pairedSenderStore.remove(pairingId)
 106:         Unit
 107:     }.onFailure { Timber.tag(TAG).e(it, "revoke pairing %s failed", pairingId) }
 108: 
 109:     private companion object {
 110:         const val TAG = "PairingRepo"
 111:     }
 112: }
 113: 
 114: data class PairingCandidate(
 115:     val brokerUrl: String,
 116:     val pairingToken: String,
 117: )

  65: async def register_bootstrap_key(
  66:     payload: BootstrapKeyRegisterRequest,
  67:     request: Request,
  68:     # Pre-auth IP bucket: cheap pre-signature DoS protection.
  69:     _: None = Depends(rate_limit("message_send_ip")),
  70:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
  71: ) -> BootstrapKeyRegisterResponse:
  72:     """V1.5 Phase 5a-2: register or rotate the sender's X25519 bootstrap
  73:     public key. The Ed25519 signature MUST be over the literal ASCII
  74:     string ``"syncler-v1-bootstrap-key:"`` (24 bytes) followed by the
  75:     raw 32-byte X25519 public key (NOT its base64 representation).
  76: 
  77:     Re-calling this endpoint rotates the key (overwrites the previous
  78:     bootstrap key + signature on the sender row). Rotation history is
  79:     not retained in V1.5 ג€” single current value per sender.
  80:     """
  81:     try:
  82:         sender = await get_active_sender(db, payload.sender_id)
  83:     except SenderNotFoundError as exc:
  84:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_404_NOT_FOUND, detail="sender not found") from exc
  85:     except SenderRevokedError as exc:
  86:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_410_GONE, detail="sender revoked") from exc
  87: 
  88:     bootstrap_key_raw = decode_base64(payload.bootstrap_key, field_name="bootstrap_key", exact=32)
  89:     bootstrap_sig_raw = decode_base64(
  90:         payload.bootstrap_key_signature, field_name="bootstrap_key_signature", exact=64,
  91:     )
  92:     sig_input = b"syncler-v1-bootstrap-key:" + bootstrap_key_raw
  93:     if not verify_message_envelope(sender.public_key, sig_input, bootstrap_sig_raw):
  94:         raise HTTPException(
  95:             status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED,
  96:             detail="invalid bootstrap key signature",
  97:         )
  98: 
  99:     # Post-signature per-sender rate limit. Mirrors plugins/publish.
 100:     request.state.sender_id = str(sender.id)
 101:     await check_rate_limit(db, request, RATE_LIMITS["bootstrap_key_register"])
 102: 
 103:     sender.bootstrap_key = bootstrap_key_raw
 104:     sender.bootstrap_key_signature = bootstrap_sig_raw
 105:     await db.commit()
 106:     await db.refresh(sender)
 107: 
 108:     bootstrap_key_id = hashlib.sha256(bootstrap_key_raw).digest()[:16]
 109:     return BootstrapKeyRegisterResponse(
 110:         bootstrap_key_id=base64.b64encode(bootstrap_key_id).decode("ascii"),
 111:     )

  50: def _b64(value: bytes) -> str:
  51:     return base64.b64encode(value).decode("ascii")
  52: 
  53: 
  54: def _b64url(value: bytes) -> str:
  55:     """URL-safe base64 (no padding) for use in URLs without percent-encoding."""
  56:     return base64.urlsafe_b64encode(value).rstrip(b"=").decode("ascii")
  57: 
  58: 
  59: def _b64url_decode(value: str) -> bytes:
  60:     pad = "=" * (-len(value) % 4)
  61:     return base64.urlsafe_b64decode(value + pad)
  62: 
  63: 
  64: def _initiate_envelope_bytes(payload: PairingInitiateRequest) -> bytes:
  65:     """Canonical bytes the sender signs to authenticate the initiate call.
  66: 
  67:     `sender_broker_url` is conditionally included: when None (V1 manual
  68:     flow), the envelope keeps the V1 3-field shape so existing senders
  69:     that don't supply a broker keep verifying. When non-None (V1.5
  70:     automated flow), it's bound into the signature so the syncler
  71:     server can't silently substitute its own URL.
  72:     """
  73:     envelope: dict = {
  74:         "sender_id": str(payload.sender_id),
  75:         "ttl_seconds": int(payload.ttl_seconds),
  76:         "metadata": payload.metadata or {},
  77:     }
  78:     if payload.sender_broker_url is not None:
  79:         envelope["sender_broker_url"] = payload.sender_broker_url
  80:     return json.dumps(envelope, sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":")).encode("utf-8")
  81: 
  82: 
  83: # V1.5 automated pairing: validation for the sender-supplied broker URL.
  84: # Spec: docs/crypto-spec.md ֲ§9. Plan: .triad/70-phase5-agreement.md.
  85: _PRIVATE_LAN_HOST_PREFIXES = ("10.", "127.", "192.168.", "172.16.", "172.17.", "172.18.", "172.19.",
  86:                               "172.20.", "172.21.", "172.22.", "172.23.", "172.24.", "172.25.",
  87:                               "172.26.", "172.27.", "172.28.", "172.29.", "172.30.", "172.31.",
  88:                               "localhost")
  89: 
  90: 
  91: def _validate_sender_broker_url(url: str, *, debug_allow_http: bool) -> None:
  92:     """Raises HTTPException(400) if the URL fails the V1.5 shape check.
  93:     Release: HTTPS only. Debug: http allowed for private LAN. No
  94:     credentials in URL, no fragment, length ג‰₪ 2048 chars, parsable.
  95:     """
  96:     from urllib.parse import urlparse
  97: 
  98:     if len(url) > 2048:
  99:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="sender_broker_url exceeds 2048 chars")
 100:     try:
 101:         parsed = urlparse(url)
 102:     except Exception as exc:
 103:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="sender_broker_url is not a valid URL") from exc
 104:     if parsed.scheme not in ("http", "https"):
 105:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="sender_broker_url scheme must be http(s)")
 106:     if parsed.username or parsed.password:
 107:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="sender_broker_url must not contain credentials")
 108:     if parsed.fragment:
 109:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="sender_broker_url must not contain a fragment")
 110:     if not parsed.hostname:
 111:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="sender_broker_url is missing a host")
 112:     if parsed.scheme == "http":
 113:         if not debug_allow_http:
 114:             raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="sender_broker_url must use HTTPS in release")
 115:         # Even in debug, only allow http for private LAN ranges so a
 116:         # dev configuration doesn't accidentally accept cleartext from
 117:         # a public sender.
 118:         if not any(parsed.hostname.startswith(p) for p in _PRIVATE_LAN_HOST_PREFIXES):
 119:             raise HTTPException(
 120:                 status_code=400,
 121:                 detail="sender_broker_url http only allowed for private LAN hosts in debug",
 122:             )
 123: 
 124: 
 125: def _bootstrap_register_envelope_bytes(payload) -> bytes:
 126:     """Canonical signing input for the bootstrap-key registration endpoint.
 127: 
 128:     Signs over the literal ASCII bytes `"syncler-v1-bootstrap-key:"` (24
 129:     bytes) followed by the raw 32-byte X25519 public key, per
 130:     `docs/crypto-spec.md ֲ§9.1`. NOT the base64 representation.
 131:     """
 132:     return b"syncler-v1-bootstrap-key:" + decode_base64(
 133:         payload.bootstrap_key, field_name="bootstrap_key", exact=32,
 134:     )
 135:

 137: @router.post("/initiate", response_model=PairingInitiateResponse, status_code=status.HTTP_201_CREATED)
 138: async def initiate(
 139:     payload: PairingInitiateRequest,
 140:     request: Request,
 141:     _: None = Depends(rate_limit("message_send_ip")),  # pre-auth IP bucket
 142:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
 143: ) -> PairingInitiateResponse:
 144:     try:
 145:         sender = await get_active_sender(db, payload.sender_id)
 146:     except SenderNotFoundError as exc:
 147:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_404_NOT_FOUND, detail="sender not found") from exc
 148:     except SenderRevokedError as exc:
 149:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_410_GONE, detail="sender revoked") from exc
 150: 
 151:     signature = decode_base64(payload.signature, field_name="signature", exact=64)
 152:     if not verify_message_envelope(sender.public_key, _initiate_envelope_bytes(payload), signature):
 153:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED, detail="invalid sender signature")
 154: 
 155:     # Post-auth per-sender bucket so an authenticated sender can't outpace us.
 156:     request.state.sender_id = str(sender.id)
 157:     await check_rate_limit(db, request, RATE_LIMITS["pairing_initiate"])
 158: 
 159:     # V1.5 automated pairing (Phase 5a-2): if the sender supplied a
 160:     # broker URL, validate shape + require the sender to have already
 161:     # registered a bootstrap key (otherwise preview can't surface the
 162:     # crypto material the device needs).
 163:     if payload.sender_broker_url is not None:
 164:         from app.config import get_settings  # local import keeps module import cheap
 165:         _validate_sender_broker_url(
 166:             payload.sender_broker_url,
 167:             debug_allow_http=(get_settings().environment == "development"),
 168:         )
 169:         if sender.bootstrap_key is None or sender.bootstrap_key_signature is None:
 170:             raise HTTPException(
 171:                 status_code=400,
 172:                 detail=(
 173:                     "sender_broker_url requires a registered bootstrap key; "
 174:                     "call POST /v1/senders/me/bootstrap-key first"
 175:                 ),
 176:             )
 177: 
 178:     pending = await initiate_pairing(
 179:         db,
 180:         sender_id=sender.id,
 181:         ttl_seconds=payload.ttl_seconds,
 182:         metadata=payload.metadata,
 183:         sender_broker_url=payload.sender_broker_url,
 184:     )
 185: 
 186:     base_url = str(request.base_url).rstrip("/")
 187:     broker_url = f"{base_url}/v1/pairing/complete?token={_b64url(pending.pairing_token)}"
 188: 
 189:     return PairingInitiateResponse(
 190:         pairing_id=pending.id,
 191:         pairing_token=_b64url(pending.pairing_token),
 192:         broker_url=broker_url,
 193:         expires_at=pending.expires_at,
 194:         sender_broker_url=payload.sender_broker_url,
 195:         bootstrap_protocol_version=(1 if payload.sender_broker_url is not None else None),
 196:     )

 199: @router.get("/preview", response_model=PairingPreviewResponse)
 200: async def preview(
 201:     token: str,
 202:     _: None = Depends(rate_limit("message_send_ip")),  # IP-based DoS hygiene
 203:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
 204: ) -> PairingPreviewResponse:
 205:     """Non-consuming sender-identity lookup. Lets the device show fingerprint
 206:     + name BEFORE the user confirms; only ``/complete`` consumes the token.
 207:     """
 208:     # Token comes URL-safe base64 (no padding); accept standard b64 too.
 209:     try:
 210:         raw = _b64url_decode(token) if not token.endswith("=") else base64.b64decode(token)
 211:     except Exception as exc:
 212:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_400_BAD_REQUEST, detail="invalid token encoding") from exc
 213:     if len(raw) != 32:
 214:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_400_BAD_REQUEST, detail="pairing token must be 32 bytes")
 215:     try:
 216:         pending, sender = await preview_pending(db, pairing_token=raw)
 217:     except PairingTokenNotFoundError as exc:
 218:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_404_NOT_FOUND, detail="pairing token not found") from exc
 219:     except PairingTokenExpiredError as exc:
 220:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_410_GONE, detail="pairing token expired") from exc
 221:     except PairingTokenConsumedError as exc:
 222:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_409_CONFLICT, detail="pairing token already consumed") from exc
 223:     except SenderRevokedError as exc:
 224:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_410_GONE, detail="sender revoked") from exc
 225: 
 226:     meta = sender_metadata_for_response(sender)
 227:     # V1.5: surface the bootstrap crypto material to the device when the
 228:     # sender opted into automated pairing. The device verifies
 229:     # `bootstrap_key_signature` against `sender_public_key` before
 230:     # encrypting anything (defense against syncler-side substitution).
 231:     bootstrap_protocol_version: int | None = None
 232:     bootstrap_key_b64: str | None = None
 233:     bootstrap_sig_b64: str | None = None
 234:     if (
 235:         pending.sender_broker_url is not None
 236:         and sender.bootstrap_key is not None
 237:         and sender.bootstrap_key_signature is not None
 238:     ):
 239:         bootstrap_protocol_version = 1
 240:         bootstrap_key_b64 = _b64(sender.bootstrap_key)
 241:         bootstrap_sig_b64 = _b64(sender.bootstrap_key_signature)
 242:     return PairingPreviewResponse(
 243:         sender_id=sender.id,
 244:         sender_name=sender.name,
 245:         sender_public_key=_b64(sender.public_key),
 246:         sender_public_key_fingerprint=meta["fingerprint"] or "",
 247:         sender_name_hash=meta["name_hash"] or "",
 248:         expires_at=pending.expires_at,
 249:         sender_broker_url=pending.sender_broker_url,
 250:         bootstrap_key=bootstrap_key_b64,
 251:         bootstrap_key_signature=bootstrap_sig_b64,
 252:         bootstrap_protocol_version=bootstrap_protocol_version,
 253:     )

 256: @router.post("/complete", response_model=PairingCompleteResponse, status_code=status.HTTP_201_CREATED)
 257: async def complete(
 258:     payload: PairingCompleteRequest,
 259:     ctx: AuthContext = Depends(current_auth_context),
 260:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
 261: ) -> PairingCompleteResponse:
 262:     # Accept URL-safe + standard base64.
 263:     raw = payload.pairing_token
 264:     try:
 265:         if "-" in raw or "_" in raw or not raw.endswith("="):
 266:             token = _b64url_decode(raw)
 267:         else:
 268:             token = base64.b64decode(raw, validate=True)
 269:     except Exception as exc:
 270:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="pairing_token must be valid base64") from exc
 271:     if len(token) != 32:
 272:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="pairing_token must decode to 32 bytes")
 273: 
 274:     encrypted_initial_state = decode_base64(
 275:         payload.encrypted_initial_state, field_name="encrypted_initial_state", minimum=16
 276:     )
 277:     try:
 278:         pairing, sender, _ = await complete_pairing(
 279:             db,
 280:             user=ctx.user,
 281:             pairing_token=token,
 282:             encrypted_initial_state=encrypted_initial_state,
 283:         )
 284:     except PairingTokenNotFoundError as exc:
 285:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_404_NOT_FOUND, detail="pairing token not found") from exc
 286:     except PairingTokenExpiredError as exc:
 287:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_410_GONE, detail="pairing token expired") from exc
 288:     except PairingTokenConsumedError as exc:
 289:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_409_CONFLICT, detail="pairing token already consumed") from exc
 290:     except SenderRevokedError as exc:
 291:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_410_GONE, detail="sender revoked") from exc
 292:     except PairingAlreadyExistsError as exc:
 293:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_409_CONFLICT, detail="already paired") from exc
 294: 
 295:     meta = sender_metadata_for_response(sender)

   1: package app.syncler.core.crypto
   2: 
   3: import java.security.MessageDigest
   4: import java.security.SecureRandom
   5: import javax.crypto.Cipher
   6: import javax.crypto.spec.GCMParameterSpec
   7: import javax.crypto.spec.SecretKeySpec
   8: import org.bouncycastle.crypto.params.X25519PrivateKeyParameters
   9: import org.bouncycastle.crypto.params.X25519PublicKeyParameters
  10: 
  11: /**
  12:  * V1.5 automated pairing bootstrap envelope.
  13:  *
  14:  * Implements the HPKE-style envelope from `docs/crypto-spec.md ֲ§9`:
  15:  *
  16:  *  1. ephemeral X25519 keypair
  17:  *  2. ECDH against the sender's bootstrap public key
  18:  *  3. HKDF-SHA256 with `salt = eph_pub || sender_bootstrap_pub` and
  19:  *     `info = "syncler-v1-bootstrap-aead"` to derive a 32-byte AES key
  20:  *  4. AES-256-GCM with a random 12-byte nonce and the canonical AAD
  21:  *
  22:  * The plaintext is `{"user_id": "...", "pairing_key": "<base64 32>"}`.
  23:  * The sender's broker reconstructs the same `aead_key` via its own
  24:  * private bootstrap key and the [ephemeralPubkey] from the wire
  25:  * envelope, then AES-GCM-decrypts.
  26:  *
  27:  * Test vectors live alongside [SpecVectorsTest]; the canonical
  28:  * Python reference is `sdk-python/syncler/bootstrap.py`. Cross-impl
  29:  * byte-equivalence is asserted in CI.
  30:  */
  31: object BootstrapEnvelope {
  32:     private const val GCM_TAG_BITS = 128
  33:     private const val GCM_NONCE_BYTES = 12
  34:     private const val X25519_KEY_BYTES = 32
  35:     private const val AEAD_KEY_BYTES = 32
  36:     private const val BOOTSTRAP_KEY_ID_BYTES = 16
  37:     private val HKDF_INFO = "syncler-v1-bootstrap-aead".encodeToByteArray()
  38: 
  39:     /**
  40:      * Build the bootstrap envelope for one pairing.
  41:      *
  42:      * Caller is responsible for sourcing the inputs from the trusted
  43:      * `pairing/preview` response (which echoes them from the sender-
  44:      * signed `pairing/initiate` envelope, so the syncler server can't
  45:      * substitute them). The bootstrap key's Ed25519 signature MUST
  46:      * be verified by the caller BEFORE invoking this method ג€”
  47:      * substitution is the threat we're guarding against.
  48:      *
  49:      * @param senderBootstrapPub the sender's raw 32-byte X25519 pub
  50:      *   key (verified-and-trusted at the call site).
  51:      * @param bootstrapKeyId the `SHA-256(senderBootstrapPub)[:16]`
  52:      *   identifier the broker uses to key its decryption state.
  53:      *   Computed locally to avoid an extra trust hop.
  54:      * @param senderBrokerUrl the URL the sender supplied to
  55:      *   `pairing/initiate`. Echoed by the server in `pairing/preview`
  56:      *   under the sender's Ed25519 signature.
  57:      * @param expIso the envelope's expiration as ISO8601 UTC with Z
  58:      *   suffix. Caller picks the value (typically `now + 60s`); broker
  59:      *   accepts a ֲ±5min window. Must use the Z suffix, not `+00:00`.
  60:      * @param plaintext canonical JSON for `{"user_id": "<uuid>",
  61:      *   "pairing_key": "<base64 32 bytes>"}`. Caller builds it.
  62:      * @param secureRandom injectable for deterministic tests; defaults
  63:      *   to platform `SecureRandom`.
  64:      */
  65:     fun build(
  66:         senderBootstrapPub: ByteArray,
  67:         pairingId: String,
  68:         senderId: String,
  69:         senderBrokerUrl: String,
  70:         expIso: String,
  71:         plaintext: ByteArray,
  72:         secureRandom: SecureRandom = SecureRandom(),
  73:     ): Envelope {
  74:         require(senderBootstrapPub.size == X25519_KEY_BYTES) {
  75:             "senderBootstrapPub must be 32 bytes, got ${senderBootstrapPub.size}"
  76:         }
  77: 
  78:         // 1. Ephemeral X25519 keypair.
  79:         val ephSeed = ByteArray(X25519_KEY_BYTES).also(secureRandom::nextBytes)
  80:         val ephPriv = X25519PrivateKeyParameters(ephSeed, 0)
  81:         val ephPub = ephPriv.generatePublicKey().encoded
  82: 
  83:         // 2. ECDH against the sender's bootstrap pub.
  84:         val sharedSecret = ByteArray(X25519_KEY_BYTES)
  85:         ephPriv.generateSecret(
  86:             X25519PublicKeyParameters(senderBootstrapPub, 0),
  87:             sharedSecret,
  88:             0,
  89:         )
  90: 
  91:         // 3. HKDF-SHA256 ג†’ aead_key (32 bytes).
  92:         val salt = ephPub + senderBootstrapPub
  93:         val aeadKey = Hkdf.deriveSha256(
  94:             ikm = sharedSecret,
  95:             salt = salt,
  96:             info = HKDF_INFO,
  97:             length = AEAD_KEY_BYTES,
  98:         )
  99: 
 100:         // 4. Canonical AAD JSON (sort_keys, ensure_ascii, compact
 101:         //    separators ג€” same encoder as message AAD ֲ§4).
 102:         val bootstrapKeyId = MessageDigest.getInstance("SHA-256")
 103:             .digest(senderBootstrapPub)
 104:             .copyOf(BOOTSTRAP_KEY_ID_BYTES)
 105:         val bootstrapKeyIdB64 = bootstrapKeyId.toBase64Std()
 106:         val aadJson = buildBootstrapAadJson(
 107:             bootstrapKeyIdB64 = bootstrapKeyIdB64,
 108:             expIso = expIso,
 109:             pairingId = pairingId,
 110:             senderBrokerUrl = senderBrokerUrl,
 111:             senderId = senderId,
 112:         )
 113: 
 114:         // 5. AES-256-GCM encrypt.
 115:         val nonce = ByteArray(GCM_NONCE_BYTES).also(secureRandom::nextBytes)
 116:         val cipher = Cipher.getInstance("AES/GCM/NoPadding")
 117:         cipher.init(
 118:             Cipher.ENCRYPT_MODE,
 119:             SecretKeySpec(aeadKey, "AES"),
 120:             GCMParameterSpec(GCM_TAG_BITS, nonce),
 121:         )
 122:         cipher.updateAAD(aadJson)
 123:         val ciphertext = cipher.doFinal(plaintext)
 124: 
 125:         return Envelope(
 126:             ephemeralPubkey = ephPub,
 127:             nonce = nonce,
 128:             ciphertext = ciphertext,
 129:             aadJson = aadJson,
 130:             bootstrapKeyIdB64 = bootstrapKeyIdB64,
 131:         )
 132:     }
 133: 
 134:     /**
 135:      * The canonical AAD JSON bytes. Visible for tests + the wire DTO
 136:      * builder. Keys MUST be in this alphabetical order; `protocol_version`
 137:      * is emitted as a JSON integer literal (no quotes); `expIso` must
 138:      * use the Z suffix. Cross-impl byte-equivalence asserted in
 139:      * `SpecVectorsTest` against `docs/crypto-spec.md ֲ§9.4`.
 140:      */
 141:     internal fun buildBootstrapAadJson(
 142:         bootstrapKeyIdB64: String,
 143:         expIso: String,
 144:         pairingId: String,
 145:         senderBrokerUrl: String,
 146:         senderId: String,
 147:     ): ByteArray = canonicalJsonBytes(
 148:         mapOf(
 149:             "bootstrap_key_id" to bootstrapKeyIdB64,
 150:             "exp" to expIso,
 151:             "pairing_id" to pairingId,
 152:             "protocol_version" to 1,
 153:             "sender_broker_url" to senderBrokerUrl,
 154:             "sender_id" to senderId,
 155:         ),
 156:     )
 157: 
 158:     /**
 159:      * Output of [build] ג€” the four fields the wire envelope carries on
 160:      * the POST body, plus [aadJson] (echoed by sender for AAD
 161:      * reconstruction sanity) and [bootstrapKeyIdB64] (the broker
 162:      * lookup key).
 163:      */
 164:     data class Envelope(
 165:         val ephemeralPubkey: ByteArray,
 166:         val nonce: ByteArray,
 167:         val ciphertext: ByteArray,
 168:         val aadJson: ByteArray,
 169:         val bootstrapKeyIdB64: String,
 170:     )
 171: }
 172: 
 173: private fun ByteArray.toBase64Std(): String =
 174:     android.util.Base64.encodeToString(this, android.util.Base64.NO_WRAP)

 succeeded in 382ms:

 151:     def create_pairing_qr(
 152:         self,
 153:         *,
 154:         ttl_seconds: int = 300,
 155:         metadata: dict[str, Any] | None = None,
 156:         out_path: str | None = None,
 157:         sender_broker_url: str | None = None,
 158:     ) -> str:
 159:         """Initiate a pairing and write a QR-code PNG of the broker URL.
 160: 
 161:         Returns the path to the generated PNG. Caller is responsible for
 162:         showing the QR to the user.
 163: 
 164:         V1.5 (Phase 5a-2): pass ``sender_broker_url`` to enable the
 165:         automated pairing flow. The Android app will POST the encrypted
 166:         bootstrap envelope to that URL after the user confirms; pair
 167:         ``Client.wait_for_pairing(...)`` against the same broker storage
 168:         you mounted the broker handler on. Pre-requisite: register the
 169:         sender's X25519 bootstrap key via
 170:         ``Client.register_bootstrap_key(...)`` before calling this with
 171:         ``sender_broker_url`` set ג€” the server rejects otherwise.
 172:         """
 173:         self._require_sender_id()
 174:         body: dict[str, Any] = {
 175:             "sender_id": self._canonical_sender_id(),
 176:             "ttl_seconds": ttl_seconds,
 177:             "metadata": metadata or {},
 178:         }
 179:         if sender_broker_url is not None:
 180:             body["sender_broker_url"] = sender_broker_url
 181:         body["signature"] = b64(self.private_key.sign(canonical_json(body)))
 182:         resp = self.session.post(f"{self.base_url}/v1/pairing/initiate", json=body, timeout=10)
 183:         resp.raise_for_status()
 184:         data = resp.json()
 185:         self._pending_pairing_token = data["pairing_token"]
 186:         self._pending_pairing_id = data["pairing_id"]
 187:         # Reserve broker storage slot when running the automated flow.
 188:         if sender_broker_url is not None and self._broker_storage is not None:
 189:             self._broker_storage.reserve(self._pending_pairing_id)
 190: 
 191:         broker_url = data["broker_url"]
 192:         out_path = out_path or f"syncler-pairing-{int(time.time())}.png"
 193:         _render_qr(broker_url, out_path)
 194:         return out_path
 195: 
 196:     def register_bootstrap_key(
 197:         self,
 198:         *,
 199:         bootstrap_public_key_raw: bytes,
 200:     ) -> str:
 201:         """V1.5 Phase 5a-2: register (or rotate) the sender's X25519
 202:         bootstrap public key. Required before calling
 203:         ``create_pairing_qr(sender_broker_url=...)``.
 204: 
 205:         Signs the literal ASCII bytes ``"syncler-v1-bootstrap-key:"``
 206:         (24 bytes) concatenated with the raw 32-byte X25519 public key,
 207:         per `docs/crypto-spec.md ֲ§9.1`. Returns the base64
 208:         ``bootstrap_key_id`` (server-computed SHA-256(pub)[:16]).
 209:         """
 210:         self._require_sender_id()
 211:         if len(bootstrap_public_key_raw) != 32:
 212:             raise ValueError("bootstrap_public_key_raw must be 32 bytes")
 213:         sig_input = b"syncler-v1-bootstrap-key:" + bootstrap_public_key_raw
 214:         signature = self.private_key.sign(sig_input)
 215:         body = {
 216:             "sender_id": self._canonical_sender_id(),
 217:             "bootstrap_key": b64(bootstrap_public_key_raw),
 218:             "bootstrap_key_signature": b64(signature),
 219:         }
 220:         resp = self.session.post(
 221:             f"{self.base_url}/v1/senders/me/bootstrap-key", json=body, timeout=10,
 222:         )
 223:         resp.raise_for_status()
 224:         return resp.json()["bootstrap_key_id"]

 226:     def wait_for_pairing(
 227:         self,
 228:         *,
 229:         timeout_seconds: int = 120,
 230:         poll_interval_seconds: float = 1.0,
 231:     ) -> Pairing:
 232:         """V1.5 Phase 5a-2: poll the broker storage until the device's
 233:         bootstrap POST lands, then automatically set the pairing on
 234:         this client.
 235: 
 236:         Defaults: 120s timeout, 1s poll with ֲ±20% jitter (jitter avoids
 237:         synchronized polling when multiple pairings are in flight).
 238:         Raises ``TimeoutError`` on deadline. Caller must have wired a
 239:         broker storage via ``Client(...)``'s constructor ג€” otherwise
 240:         there's nothing to poll.
 241:         """
 242:         import random
 243:         if self._broker_storage is None:
 244:             raise SynclerError(
 245:                 "wait_for_pairing requires a broker storage. Pass one to "
 246:                 "Client(broker_storage=InMemoryBrokerStorage()) at construction time.",
 247:             )
 248:         if self._pending_pairing_id is None:
 249:             raise SynclerError(
 250:                 "no pending pairing ג€” call create_pairing_qr(sender_broker_url=...) first",
 251:             )
 252:         deadline = time.monotonic() + timeout_seconds
 253:         while True:
 254:             entry = self._broker_storage.fetch(self._pending_pairing_id)
 255:             if entry is not None:
 256:                 pairing = Pairing(
 257:                     pairing_id=self._pending_pairing_id,
 258:                     user_id=entry.user_id,
 259:                 )
 260:                 self._latest_pairing = pairing
 261:                 self.pairing_key = entry.pairing_key
 262:                 return pairing
 263:             remaining = deadline - time.monotonic()
 264:             if remaining <= 0:
 265:                 raise TimeoutError(
 266:                     f"wait_for_pairing exceeded {timeout_seconds}s timeout",
 267:                 )
 268:             jitter = poll_interval_seconds * 0.2 * (random.random() * 2 - 1)
 269:             sleep_for = min(remaining, max(0.05, poll_interval_seconds + jitter))
 270:             time.sleep(sleep_for)
 271:

 273:         """Dev-mode shortcut: set the paired user_id and per-pairing AES key.
 274: 
 275:         Production flow has the device exchange this key with the sender

  58: def assemble_bootstrap_aad(
  59:     *,
  60:     bootstrap_key_id_b64: str,
  61:     exp_iso: str,
  62:     pairing_id: str,
  63:     sender_broker_url: str,
  64:     sender_id: str,
  65: ) -> bytes:
  66:     """Canonical AAD bytes for the V1.5 bootstrap envelope.
  67: 
  68:     Spec: ֲ§9.3. Keys are sorted alphabetically; `protocol_version` is
  69:     a JSON integer literal (no quotes); `exp_iso` must use the `Z`
  70:     suffix. ``sender_broker_url`` MUST be sourced from the broker's
  71:     trusted storage for ``pairing_id`` (NOT echoed from any client-
  72:     supplied envelope field) ג€” otherwise a syncler-server substitution
  73:     attack is possible.
  74:     """
  75:     return json.dumps(
